# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/terraform--a3dc5711` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/terraform--a3dc5711$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture Documentation

## Objective

Generate comprehensive architecture documentation for Terraform's plan/apply pipeline. Your documentation should explain how Terraform executes the plan and apply operations, covering the internal components and their interactions.

## Scope

Your documentation should cover the following architectural components:

1. **Graph Builder System**
   - How the dependency graph is constructed
   - The role of graph transformers in building the execution graph
   - How resources, providers, and modules are represented as graph nodes
   - How dependencies between resources are discovered and encoded as edges

2. **Provider Interface and Lifecycle**
   - How providers are initialized and managed during execution
   - The provider plugin architecture
   - How resource operations are delegated to providers
   - Provider configuration and instance management

3. **State Management**
   - How state is read, modified, and persisted during plan/apply
   - The role of state managers and state synchronization
   - How state snapshots enable concurrent graph evaluation
   - State locking and remote state backends

4. **Execution Flow and Hook System**
   - The overall execution flow from command invocation to completion
   - How graph nodes are evaluated (plan vs apply execution)
   - The walker pattern for graph traversal
   - Hook points for extending Terraform's behavior
   - Dynamic expansion for count/for_each resources

## Requirements

- **Component Responsibilities**: Clearly explain what each major component does
- **Data Flow**: Describe how data flows through the system during plan and apply operations
- **Extension Points**: Identify where the architecture allows for customization or extension
- **Error Handling**: Explain how errors are propagated and handled during execution

## Deliverable

Write your documentation to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format.

Your documentation should be technical and precise, aimed at developers who want to understand Terraform's internal architecture. Include specific details about component interactions, not just high-level descriptions.

## Success Criteria

Your documentation will be evaluated on:
- Coverage of all required architectural topics
- Accurate description of component responsibilities and interactions
- Clear explanation of data flow through the pipeline
- Identification of key extension points in the architecture
- Technical depth appropriate for internal architecture documentation

Excellent! I've successfully created comprehensive architecture documentation for Terraform's plan/apply pipeline. Here's what the documentation covers:

## Documentation Structure

**File**: `/workspace/documentation.md` (35KB, 1126 lines)

### Content Overview

1. **Graph Builder System** - How the dependency graph is constructed using a transformer pipeline architecture
   - Graph structure and validation
   - Builder interfaces and implementations
   - Phase-specific builders (Plan vs Apply)
   - Graph transformers for adding/filtering/ordering nodes
   - Node abstraction and concrete conversion

2. **Provider Interface and Lifecycle** - How providers are managed and invoked
   - Lazy initialization and caching
   - Configuration merging (explicit + user input + parent)
   - Plugin architecture and gRPC communication
   - Resource operation delegation patterns

3. **State Management** - How state is safely managed during concurrent execution
   - Hierarchical state structure (modules, resources, instances)
   - `SyncState` wrapper for thread-safe access with RWMutex
   - Multiple state versions (State, RefreshState, PrevRunState)
   - Atomic operations and deep copying for consistency
   - Backend persistence and locking

4. **Execution Flow and Hook System** - Complete execution pipeline with extension points
   - Plan execution: refresh → diff → plan
   - Apply execution: graph build → apply walk → state update
   - DAG walker with parallel execution respecting dependencies
   - 15+ hook points for observation and control
   - Dynamic expansion for count/for_each during execution

5. **Evaluation Context** - Runtime environment for node execution
   - EvalContext interface for provider, state, and config access
   - Expression evaluation and scope management
   -

The caller must\n118: \t// coordinate a lock for the state if necessary, such that the Hook may\n119: \t// access it freely without any need for additional locks to protect from\n120: \t// concurrent writes. Implementations which modify or retain the state after\n121: \t// the call has returned must copy the state.\n122: \tPostStateUpdate(new *states.State) (HookAction, error)\n123: }\n124: \n125: // NilHook is a Hook implementation that does nothing.     "content": "1: // Copyright (c) HashiCorp, Inc.\n2: // SPDX-License-Identifier: BUSL-1.1\n3: \n4: package states\n5: \n6: import (\n7: \t\"log\"\n8: \t\"sync\"\n9: \n10: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/addrs\"\n11: \t\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/checks\"\n12: \t\"github.com/zclconf/go-cty/cty\"\n13: )\n14: \n15: // SyncState is a wrapper around State that provides concurrency-safe access to\n16: // various common operations that occur during a Terraform graph walk, or other\n17: // similar concurrent contexts.\n18: //\n19: // When a SyncState wrapper is in use, no concurrent direct access to the\n20: // underlying objects is permitted unless the caller first acquires an explicit\n21: // lock, using the Lock and Unlock methods. Most callers should _not_\n22: // explicitly lock, and should instead use the other methods of this type that\n23: // handle locking automatically.\n24: //\n25: // Since SyncState is able to safely consolidate multiple updates into a single\n26: // atomic operation, many of its methods are at a higher level than those\n27: // of the underlying types, and operate on the state as a whole rather than\n28: // on individual sub-structures of the state.\n29: //\n30: // SyncState can only protect against races within its own methods. It cannot\n31: // provide any guarantees about the order in which concurrent operations will\n32: // be processed, so callers may still need to employ higher-level techniques\n33: // for ensuring correct operation sequencing, such as building and walking\n34: // a dependency graph.\n35: type SyncState struct {\n36: \tstate    *State\n37: \twritable bool\n38: \tlock     sync.RWMutex\n39: }\n40: \n41: // Module returns a snapshot of the state of the module instance with the given\n42: // address, or nil if no such module is tracked.\n43: //\n44: // The return value is a pointer to a copy of the module state, which the\n45: // caller may then freely access and mutate. However, since the module state\n46: // tends to be a large data structure with many child objects, where possible\n47: // callers should prefer to use a more granular accessor to access a child\n48: // module directly, and thus reduce the amount of copying required.\n49: func (s *SyncState) Module(addr addrs.ModuleInstance) *Module {\n50: \ts.lock.RLock()\n51: \tret := s.state.Module(addr).DeepCopy()\n52: \ts.lock.RUnlock()\n53: \treturn ret\n54: }\n55: \n56: // RemoveModule removes the entire state for the given module, taking with\n57: // it any resources associated with the module. Input
{
  "content": "# Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform's plan and apply operations are executed through a sophisticated graph-based execution engine. The architecture decomposes these operations into two major phases:\n\n1. **Graph Construction Phase**: Builds a directed acyclic graph (DAG) representing resources, their configurations, and their dependencies\n2. **Graph Execution Phase**: Traverses the graph respecting dependencies, executing operations in parallel where possible\n\nThis document details the internal architecture of these components and their interactions.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Graph Builder System\n\n### 1.1 Core Graph Structure\n\nThe `Graph` type represents the execution plan as a directed acyclic graph with the following structure:\n\n```\nGraph\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 dag.AcyclicGraph (embedded)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 Path: addrs.ModuleInstance  // Module scope for this graph\n```\n\n**Key Responsibilities:**\n- Maintains graph vertices (nodes) and edges (dependencies)\n- Validates that the graph is acyclic and has a single root\n- Provides traversal capabilities via the embedded `AcyclicGraph`\n- Supports concurrent graph walks through the `Walk()` method\n\n### 1.2 GraphBuilder Interface\n\nThe `GraphBuilder` interface defines how graphs are constructed:\n\n```go\ntype GraphBuilder interface {\n    Build(addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n}\n```\n\nThe standard implementation is `BasicGraphBuilder`, which:\n- Maintains an ordered list of `GraphTransformer` steps\n- Executes each transformer in sequence, modifying the graph incrementally\n- Validates the final graph for cycles and connectivity\n- Logs graph state changes after each transformation step\n\n**Execution Pattern:**\n```\nGraphBuilder.Build()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Create empty Graph\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 For each GraphTransformer in Steps:\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Call Transform(graph)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Log graph state\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Handle errors\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 Validate graph (single root, no cycles)\n```\n\n### 1.3 Phase-Specific Graph Builders\n\n#### PlanGraphBuilder\n\nConstructs the execution graph for plan operations. Key characteristics:\n\n- **Source of Truth**: Configuration (desired state) combined with current state\n- **Decisions Based On**: Diff between prior state and configuration\n- **Does NOT Consider**: Lifecycle preferences like `create_before_destroy` (these are post-plan concerns)\n\n**Key Fields:**\n- `Config`: Configuration tree representing desired state\n- `State`: Current state\n- `RootVariableValues`: Input variables provided by user\n- `Targets`: Resource targeting filters\n- `ForceReplace`: Resources to force replacement\n- `Plugins`: Provider and provisioner factory references\n\n#### ApplyGraphBuilder\n\nConstructs the execution graph for apply operations. Key characteristics:\n\n- **Source of Truth**: The Plan object (list of changes)\n- **Protects Against**: Applying resources not explicitly in the plan\n- **Decisions Based On**: The calculated changes from planning\n\n**Key Fields:**\n- `Config`: Configuration (must match the plan's source config)\n- `Changes`: The plan changes to apply\n- `State`: Current state before applying changes\n- `Targets`: Resource targeting filters (for consistency checking)\n\n### 1.4 Graph Transformers\n\nGraph transformers implement the `GraphTransformer` interface:\n\n```go\ntype GraphTransformer interface {\n    Transform(*Graph) error\n}\n```\n\nTransformers incrementally build the execution graph by:\n1. **Adding nodes**: Creating graph vertices representing resources, providers, modules, etc.\n2. **Creating edges**: Establishing dependency relationships\n3. **Filtering**: Removing nodes that shouldn't be executed\n4. **Expanding**: Converting abstract nodes to concrete operational nodes\n\n#### Key Transformer Categories\n\n**Configuration Transformers:**\n- `ConfigTransformer`: Adds all resources from configuration to graph\n- `AttachConfigProviderTransformer`: Attaches provider configuration to nodes\n- `AttachConfigResourceTransformer`: Attaches resource configuration to resource nodes\n- `AttachSchemaTransformer`: Adds provider schemas for validation\n\n**State Transformers:**\n- `AttachStateTransformer`: Attaches prior state to resource nodes\n- `StateTransformer`: Adds state-only resources not in configuration (for cleanup)\n\n**Expansion Transformers:**\n- `ExpandTransformer`: Expands `count` and `for_each` resources into concrete instances\n- `ModuleExpansionTransformer`: Expands module calls into concrete module instances\n- These are critical for dynamic expansion during execution\n\n**Dependency Transformers:**\n- `ReferenceTransformer`: Builds edges based on resource references in expressions\n- `ProviderTransformer`: Adds provider nodes and establishes provider dependencies\n- `DestroyEdgeTransformer`: Creates special edges for resource destruction order\n- `DestroyCreateBeforeDestroyTransformer`: Implements lifecycle rules\n\n**Filtering Transformers:**\n- `TargetsTransformer`: Filters graph to only targeted resources and their dependencies\n- `OrphanTransformer`: Marks resources for destruction if removed from configuration\n- `TransitiveReductionTransformer`: Removes redundant edges to simplify execution\n\n**Ordering Transformers:**\n- `ImportStateTransformer`: Adds import operations\n- `CheckTransformer`: Adds check validation nodes\n- `VariableValidationTransformer`: Adds variable validation nodes\n\n### 1.5 Node Types and Abstraction\n\n#### Abstract Nodes\n\nAbstract nodes are transitional node types that represent the logical concept of an operation without being executable:\n\n- `NodeAbstractResource`: Base for resource-level operations\n- `NodeAbstractResourceInstance`: Base for single resource instance operations\n- `NodeAbstractProvider`: Base for provider operations\n- `NodeAbstractModule`: Base for module operations\n\n**Concrete Node Conversion:**\n\nThe graph builder uses factory functions to convert abstract nodes to concrete, executable types:\n\n```go\n// Factory function signature\ntype ConcreteResourceInstanceNodeFunc func(*NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex\n\n// Usage in builders\nconcreteResourceInstance := func(a *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex {\n    return &NodeApplyableResourceInstance{\n        NodeAbstractResourceInstance: a,\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis allows the same abstract representation to be converted to different executable nodes depending on the operation (plan vs apply).\n\n#### Concrete Node Examples\n\n- `NodeApplyableResource`: Expansion node for apply phase\n- `NodePlanResourceInstance`: Plans changes for a resource instance\n- `NodeApplyableResourceInstance`: Applies a change to a resource instance\n- `NodeDestroyResourceInstance`: Destroys a resource instance\n- `NodeRefreshResourceInstance`: Refreshes a resource instance's state\n- `NodeApplyableProvider`: Initializes and configures a provider\n- `NodeDataSource`: Reads a data source\n- `NodeOutput`: Computes output values\n\n---\n\n## 2. Provider Interface and Lifecycle\n\n### 2.1 Provider Initialization and Management\n\nProviders are lazily initialized during graph execution through the `EvalContext` interface.\n\n#### Initialization Sequence\n\n```\n1. Provider node execution begins\n2. EvalContext.InitProvider(addr, config) called\n3. Provider plugin loaded and instantiated\n4. Provider schema retrieved from plugin\n5. Provider stored in cache for reuse\n6. Subsequent references use cached provider\n```\n\n#### Key EvalContext Methods for Providers\n\n```go\ntype EvalContext interface {\n    // Initialize a provider with configuration\n    InitProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config *configs.Provider)\n        (providers.Interface, error)\n\n    // Retrieve already-initialized provider\n    Provider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) providers.Interface\n\n    // Get provider schema (must already be initialized)\n    ProviderSchema(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) (providers.ProviderSchema, error)\n\n    // Close provider connections when done\n    CloseProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) error\n\n    // Configure provider with merged config\n    ConfigureProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config cty.Value) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n### 2.2 Provider Configuration and Input\n\nProvider configuration is built by merging multiple sources:\n\n```\nProvider Configuration = User Input + Explicit Config + Parent Config\n```\n\n**Priority Order:**\n1. User input from interactive prompts (highest priority)\n2. Explicit configuration from HCL\n3. Parent provider configuration (for child modules)\n\nThe `buildProviderConfig()` function handles this merging:\n\n```go\nfunc buildProviderConfig(ctx EvalContext, addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig,\n    config *configs.Provider) hcl.Body {\n    // Merge input and explicit config\n    // User input takes priority\n}\n```\n\n### 2.3 Provider Plugin Architecture\n\nProviders are external plugins communicating via gRPC. The plugin lifecycle:\n\n1. **Discovery**: Providers found in `.terraform/plugins` or installed via provider requirements\n2. **Loading**: Plugin binary launched as subprocess\n3. **Handshake**: Protocol negotiation and capability discovery\n4. **Schema Fetch**: Request provider schema definition\n5. **Configuration**: Provider receives merged configuration\n6. **Resource Operations**: Provider executes Create/Read/Update/Delete operations\n7. **Cleanup**: Provider process terminates when `CloseProvider()` called\n\n### 2.4 Resource Operation Delegation\n\nWhen a resource operation is planned or applied:\n\n```\nNode.Execute()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Get provider from EvalContext\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Request resource schema from provider\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Build request object (state + config)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Call provider method (PlanResourceChange, ApplyResourceChange, etc.)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Capture response (planned/new state, error)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 Update local state with response\n```\n\nEach provider method is responsible for:\n- Validating arguments\n- Computing differences (for Plan)\n- Making API calls\n- Handling errors\n- Returning updated resource state\n\n---\n\n## 3. State Management\n\n### 3.1 State Structure\n\nThe `State` type represents Terraform's persistent state:\n\n```\nState\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Modules: map[string]*Module\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Module (for each module instance)\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 Resources: map[string]*Resource\n\u2502       \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Resource\n\u2502       \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 Instances: map[addrs.InstanceKey]*ResourceInstance\n\u2502       \u2502           \u2514\u2500\u2500 ResourceInstance\n\u2502       \u2502               \u251c\u2500\u2500 Current: *ResourceInstanceObject\n\u2502       \u2502               \u2514\u2500\u2500 Deposed: map[DeposedKey]*ResourceInstanceObject\n\u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 Outputs: map[string]*OutputValue\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 RootOutputValues: map[string]*OutputValue\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 CheckResults: *CheckResults\n```\n\n**Key Properties:**\n- **Hierarchical**: Organized by modules and resources\n- **Instance-Based**: Resources can have multiple instances (count/for_each)\n- **Deposed Objects**: Tracks old objects during create-before-destroy operations\n- **Immutable Interface**: State should only be modified through `SyncState` methods\n\n### 3.2 State Synchronization (SyncState)\n\nFor concurrent graph execution, state is wrapped in `SyncState`:\n\n```go\ntype SyncState struct {\n    state    *State\n    writable bool\n    lock     sync.RWMutex  // Protects concurrent access\n}\n```\n\n**Features:**\n- Atomic operations: Multiple state changes happen together or not at all\n- Read-Write separation: Multiple readers or single writer\n- Deep copying: Returned values are independent copies\n- Automatic pruning: Empty modules are removed (except root)\n\n**High-Level Operations:**\n\n```go\n// Resource instance operations\nSetResourceInstanceCurrent(addr, obj, provider)\nDeposeResourceInstanceObject(addr) DeposedKey\nSetResourceInstanceDeposed(addr, key, obj, provider)\n\n// Output operations\nSetOutputValue(addr, value, sensitive)\nRemoveOutputValue(addr)\n\n// Module operations\nRemoveModule(addr)\n\n// Batch operations for planning\nUpdateResourceInstanceObjects(...)\n```\n\n**Benefits:**\n- Enables concurrent graph node execution without race conditions\n- Provides consistent snapshots for reading\n- Prevents partial state updates during failures\n\n### 3.3 Multiple State Versions During Execution\n\nTerraform maintains multiple state objects simultaneously during a walk:\n\n```\nState: Current state being built\n    \u2191\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 Updated by Apply/Plan nodes\n\nRefreshState: State after refresh phase\n    \u2191\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 Populated during refresh walk\n\nPrevRunState: State from previous run\n    \u2191\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 Loaded at start, used for comparison\n```\n\n**Usage:**\n- `State`: Primary state being modified\n- `RefreshState`: Previous state snapshot (for change detection)\n- `PrevRunState`: Used for comparisons and understanding drift\n\nThis enables:\n- Change detection: Compare current vs previous state\n- Rollback capability: Previous state preserved\n- Consistency checking: Ensure applied changes match plan\n\n### 3.4 State Persistence and Backends\n\nState management is abstracted through the state manager interface in `statemgr` package:\n\n```\nBackend (e.g., S3, Azure Storage)\n    \u2191\nState Manager (implements locking, versioning)\n    \u2191\nLocal State File (JSON format)\n```\n\n**Key Responsibilities:**\n- **Reading**: Load state from backend\n- **Locking**: Prevent concurrent operations\n- **Versioning**: Track state history\n- **Persistence**: Write updated state back to backend\n\nThe Context holds a reference to the state manager for:\n- Initial state loading\n- Atomic write-back after successful apply\n- Lock management during operations\n\n---\n\n## 4. Execution Flow and Hook System\n\n### 4.1 Overall Plan Execution Flow\n\n```\nContext.Plan(config, opts)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 1. Build Plan Graph\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 PlanGraphBuilder.Build()\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Apply transformers in sequence\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Return executable Graph\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 2. Refresh Walk (optional)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Walk graph with RefreshWalker\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Call resource ReadState for current values\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Update RefreshState with current values\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Returns refreshed state for comparison\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 3. Plan Walk\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Walk graph with PlanWalker\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 For each resource node:\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Call provider.PlanResourceChange()\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Capture planned change (Create/Update/Delete/NoOp)\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Store in Changes\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Returns complete change set\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500 4. Return Plan Object\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 Contains all changes ready for apply\n```\n\n### 4.2 Overall Apply Execution Flow\n\n```\nContext.Apply(plan, config, opts)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 1. Build Apply Graph\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 ApplyGraphBuilder.Build(plan.Changes)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Only includes changed resources\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Applies create-before-destroy ordering\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Return executable Graph\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 2. Apply Walk\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Walk graph with ApplyWalker\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 For each resource change node:\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Call provider resource operation (Create/Update/Delete)\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Update state with result\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Call hooks (PreApply, PostApply)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Handle deposed objects cleanup\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Update State atomically\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500 3. Return Updated State\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 State persisted to backend\n```\n\n### 4.3 Graph Traversal (Walker)\n\nThe DAG walker executes nodes respecting dependencies:\n\n```\nWalker Algorithm:\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 For each vertex (node) in graph:\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Wait for all dependencies to complete\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 If dependency failed: Skip or error (per graph semantics)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Execute node callback (concurrent if possible)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Collect diagnostics\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Mark vertex complete\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500 Return aggregated diagnostics from all vertices\n```\n\n**Key Walker Characteristics:**\n- **Parallel Execution**: Independent nodes execute concurrently\n- **Dependency Respect**: Nodes only execute after upstream dependencies complete\n- **Atomic Failures**: Failed nodes block downstream dependents\n- **Cancelable**: Graph walk can be stopped via context cancellation\n\n### 4.4 Execution in ContextGraphWalker\n\nThe `ContextGraphWalker` implements the Terraform-specific walker pattern:\n\n```go\ntype ContextGraphWalker struct {\n    Context              *Context\n    State                *states.SyncState    // Main state\n    RefreshState         *states.SyncState    // Pre-walk state snapshot\n    Changes              *plans.ChangesSync   // Accumulates changes\n    Checks               *checks.State\n    NamedValues          *namedvals.State     // Variable/output tracking\n    InstanceExpander     *instances.Expander  // Count/for_each expansion\n    Operation            walkOperation\n    StopContext          context.Context\n}\n\n// Key method called for each node\nfunc (w *ContextGraphWalker) Execute(ctx EvalContext, node GraphNodeExecutable) {\n    // Acquire parallelism semaphore\n    w.Context.parallelSem.Acquire()\n    defer w.Context.parallelSem.Release()\n\n    // Execute the node\n    return node.Execute(ctx, w.Operation)\n}\n```\n\n**Scope Management:**\n\nThe walker maintains multiple evaluation contexts, one per module:\n\n```go\nfunc (w *ContextGraphWalker) enterScope(scope evalContextScope) EvalContext {\n    // Returns EvalContext scoped to a specific module\n    // Caches contexts to ensure consistency\n}\n```\n\nThis allows:\n- Module isolation\n- Variable scope containment\n- Provider configuration inheritance\n\n### 4.5 Hook System\n\nHooks are callback points allowing external code to observe and influence execution.\n\n#### Hook Interface\n\n```go\ntype Hook interface {\n    // Resource operation hooks\n    PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        newState cty.Value, err error) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Plan hooks\n    PreDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        priorState, proposedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Provisioning hooks\n    PreProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PreProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string, err error) (HookAction, error)\n    ProvisionOutput(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string, line string)\n\n    // State refresh hooks\n    PreRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState, newState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Import hooks\n    PreImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, importID string) (HookAction, error)\n    PostImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, imported []providers.ImportedResource) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Lifecycle hooks\n    PostStateUpdate(new *states.State) (HookAction, error)\n    Stopping()\n}\n```\n\n#### Hook Actions\n\n```go\ntype HookAction byte\n\nconst (\n    HookActionContinue  // Proceed normally\n    HookActionHalt      // Cancel operation\n)\n```\n\n#### Hook Execution Flow\n\n```\nFor each hook in Context.hooks:\n    Call hook method with resource details\n    \u251c\u2500 HookActionContinue: Proceed to next hook\n    \u2514\u2500 HookActionHalt: Cancel operation, stop remaining hooks\n```\n\n#### Common Hook Uses\n\n1. **UI Output**: Display resource operations and status\n2. **Logging**: Track operations for audit\n3. **Monitoring**: Integrate with external systems\n4. **Validation**: Custom checks during apply\n5. **Deferral**: Implement custom pause/resume logic\n\n### 4.6 Dynamic Expansion During Execution\n\nCount and for_each resources are expanded dynamically during graph execution.\n\n#### Instance Expansion\n\n```\nInstance Expander tracks:\n\u251c\u2500 count.index / each.key / each.value for current iteration\n\u251c\u2500 length calculations for count\n\u251c\u2500 map iterations for for_each\n\u2514\u2500 Nested expansion for resource instances\n```\n\n**Expansion Process:**\n\n```\n1. InstanceExpander node executes\n   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Evaluates count or for_each expression\n   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Creates abstract instances for each value\n\n2. Instance keys created: IntKey for count, StringKey for for_each\n\n3. Per-instance nodes created from abstract node\n   \u251c\u2500\u2500 NodeResourcePlanInstance\n   \u251c\u2500\u2500 NodeResourceApplyInstance\n   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Can access instance key for self references\n\n4. Instances execute in graph order\n   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Each instance has independent state/attributes\n```\n\n**Data Available to Instances:**\n\n```\nself.*              // Current resource's computed attributes\ncount.index         // Numeric index (count)\neach.key            // Map key (for_each)\neach.value          // Map value (for_each)\nresource.*.id       // Splat referencing other instances\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Evaluation Context\n\n### 5.1 EvalContext Interface\n\nThe `EvalContext` is the primary interface for node execution, providing access to:\n\n```go\ntype EvalContext interface {\n    // Module and path information\n    Path() addrs.ModuleInstance\n    Stopped() <-chan struct{}\n\n    // Provider operations\n    InitProvider(addr, config) providers.Interface\n    Provider(addr) providers.Interface\n    ProviderSchema(addr) providers.ProviderSchema\n    CloseProvider(addr) error\n    ConfigureProvider(addr, config) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n    // Provisioners\n    Provisioner(name) provisioners.Interface\n    ProvisionerSchema(name) *configschema.Block\n\n    // State and changes\n    State() *states.SyncState\n    RefreshState() *states.SyncState\n    Changes() *plans.ChangesSync\n    NamedValues() *namedvals.State\n\n    // Expression evaluation\n    EvaluateBlock(body, schema, self, key) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n    EvaluateExpr(expr, wantType, self) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n    EvaluationScope(self, source, key) *lang.Scope\n\n    // Hooks and plugins\n    Hook(callback func(Hook) error) error\n    Input() UIInput\n}\n```\n\n### 5.2 BuiltinEvalContext Implementation\n\nThe standard implementation provides:\n\n```go\ntype BuiltinEvalContext struct {\n    // Execution environment\n    StopContext  context.Context\n    InstanceExpander *instances.Expander\n\n    // Caches\n    ProviderCache      map[string]providers.Interface\n    ProvisionerCache   map[string]provisioners.Interface\n\n    // State and configuration\n    StateValue         *states.SyncState\n    ChangesValue       *plans.ChangesSync\n    ChecksValue        *checks.State\n    NamedValuesValue   *namedvals.State\n    DeferralsValue     *deferring.Deferred\n\n    // Configuration\n    ConfigValue        *configs.Config\n    PluginsValue       *contextPlugins\n\n    // Evaluation\n    EvaluatorValue     *Evaluator\n}\n```\n\n**Key Responsibilities:**\n- Maintains caches for provider/provisioner instances\n- Coordinates access to state and changes\n- Provides expression evaluation capabilities\n- Manages hook invocation\n\n### 5.3 Evaluation and Expression Handling\n\nThe `Evaluator` handles HCL expression evaluation:\n\n```\nExpression Evaluation:\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Parse expression as HCL\n\u251c\u2500 Build evaluation scope with:\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Module variables\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Local values\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Resource references\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Data source references\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Functions and operators\n\u251c\u2500 Execute evaluation in scope\n\u251c\u2500 Apply type conversion if needed\n\u2514\u2500 Return evaluated cty.Value\n```\n\n**Scope Includes:**\n- `self.*`: Current resource or data source\n- Variables from root and current module\n- Outputs from all modules\n- Data source read values\n- Locals from current module\n- References to other resources/data sources\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points\n\n### 6.1 Custom Transformers\n\nExtend graph building by implementing `GraphTransformer`:\n\n```go\ntype CustomTransformer struct {\n    // Configuration\n}\n\nfunc (t *CustomTransformer) Transform(g *Graph) error {\n    // Add, remove, or modify nodes and edges\n    return nil\n}\n\n// Register with graph builder\nbuilder.Steps = append(builder.Steps, &CustomTransformer{})\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Custom node scheduling\n- Integration-specific resource ordering\n- Cost optimization by graph reordering\n- Security enforcement via forced dependencies\n\n### 6.2 Custom Hooks\n\nImplement `Hook` interface to observe execution:\n\n```go\ntype CustomHook struct{\n}\n\nfunc (h *CustomHook) PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, ...) (HookAction, error) {\n    // Log, validate, or modify behavior\n    return HookActionContinue, nil\n}\n\n// Register with context\nopts.Hooks = append(opts.Hooks, &CustomHook{})\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Real-time operation monitoring\n- Cost estimation\n- Resource validation\n- Event forwarding to external systems\n- Custom approval workflows\n\n### 6.3 Provider Plugins\n\nProviders are the primary extension point. Implement the `providers.Interface`:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    GetSchema(ctx context.Context) (*ProviderSchema, error)\n    PrepareProviderConfig(ctx context.Context, req PrepareProviderConfigRequest) PrepareProviderConfigResponse\n    ValidateResourceConfig(ctx context.Context, req ValidateResourceConfigRequest) ValidateResourceConfigResponse\n    ReadResource(ctx context.Context, req ReadResourceRequest) ReadResourceResponse\n    PlanResourceChange(ctx context.Context, req PlanResourceChangeRequest) PlanResourceChangeResponse\n    ApplyResourceChange(ctx context.Context, req ApplyResourceChangeRequest) ApplyResourceChangeResponse\n    // ... more methods\n}\n```\n\n**Hook Points:**\n- Configuration validation\n- Resource diffing\n- Resource creation, update, deletion\n- State refresh\n- Data source reads\n\n### 6.4 Custom Provisioners\n\nImplement `provisioners.Interface` for post-apply provisioning:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    GetSchema(ctx context.Context) (*configschema.Block, error)\n    ProvisionResource(ctx context.Context, req ProvisionResourceRequest) ProvisionResourceResponse\n    Stop(ctx context.Context) error\n}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Configuration management (Ansible, Chef, Puppet)\n- Custom deployment scripts\n- Infrastructure validation\n- Service registration\n\n---\n\n## 7. Error Handling\n\n### 7.1 Error Propagation\n\nErrors are collected and propagated through the execution flow:\n\n```\nNode.Execute() returns tfdiags.Diagnostics\n    \u2193\nDiagnostic collected in walker\n    \u2193\nWalker stops dependent nodes\n    \u2193\nAggregated diagnostics returned to caller\n```\n\n**Diagnostic Types:**\n- `Error`: Prevents operation and downstream nodes\n- `Warning`: Logged but doesn't block execution\n- `Detail`: Informational messages\n\n### 7.2 Failure Handling in Parallel Execution\n\nWhen a node fails:\n\n1. **Downstream Blocking**: Dependent nodes receive error signal and don't execute\n2. **Parallel Sibling Isolation**: Independent nodes continue executing\n3. **Partial Completion**: Some resources may have executed before failure\n4. **State Preservation**: State partially updated with successful operations\n\n**Recovery Strategy:**\n- User can fix error and rerun plan/apply\n- Partial state is not persisted without full success\n- Deferred resources allow deferring problematic resources to next run\n\n### 7.3 Non-Fatal Errors\n\nSome errors don't block execution:\n\n```go\ntype NonFatalError interface {\n    Diagnostics() tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\nThese allow:\n- Collection of multiple issues\n- User fixing issues in one pass\n- Proceeding with partial results when appropriate\n\n---\n\n## 8. Data Flow Diagram\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Configuration  \u2502\n\u2502   (HCL files)   \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n         \u2502\n         v\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Config Loader          \u2502\n\u2502  (parses, validates)    \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n         \u2502\n         v\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 Graph Builder           \u2502\n\u2502 (PlanGraphBuilder)      \u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2524\n\u2502 Steps:                  \u2502\n\u2502 1. ConfigTransformer    \u2502\n\u2502 2. ExpandTransformer    \u2502\n\u2502 3. ReferenceTransformer \u2502\n\u2502 4. ProviderTransformer  \u2502\n\u2502 5. ... \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n---\n\n## 9. Performance Considerations\n\n### 9.1 Parallelism\n\nGraph execution naturally parallelizes:\n\n**Without Dependencies**: 100 independent resources execute concurrently (up to parallelism limit)\n\n**With Dependencies**: Resources execute in dependency order, but siblings execute in parallel\n\n```\nExample:\naws_vpc.main (Parallelism: 1/10)\n\u251c\u2500 aws_subnet.a (Parallelism: 2/10)\n\u251c\u2500 aws_subnet.b (Parallelism: 3/10)\n\u2514\u2500 aws_subnet.c (Parallelism: 4/10)\n   \u251c\u2500 aws_instance.1 (Parallelism: 5/10)\n   \u251c\u2500 aws_instance.2 (Parallelism: 6/10)\n   \u2514\u2500 aws_instance.3 (Parallelism: 7/10)\n```\n\n### 9.2 State Access Optimization\n\n`SyncState` minimizes lock contention:\n\n- Atomic operations reduce lock time\n- Deep copies prevent concurrent mutations\n- Module-level granularity allows targeting\n- Read-write separation maximizes parallelism\n\n### 9.3 Graph Construction Time\n\nLarge graphs (100s of resources) build in milliseconds:\n\n- Transformers run sequentially (single-threaded)\n- Most transformers run in O(n) or O(n log n)\n- TransitiveReduction can be expensive (O(VE)) but optional\n\n### 9.4 Execution Time Optimization Opportunities\n\n1. **Targeted apply**: Only resources with changes\n2. **Parallelism tuning**: `-parallelism=N` flag\n3. **Resource ordering**: Explicit `depends_on` for critical paths\n4. **Deferred actions**: Postpone problematic resources\n5. **Caching**: Provider schemas cached, reused across module instances\n\n---\n\n## 10. Key Architectural Patterns\n\n### 10.1 Builder Pattern\n\nThe `BasicGraphBuilder` + `GraphTransformer` chain:\n\n```\nEmpty Graph \u2192 Step 1 \u2192 Step 2 \u2192 ... \u2192 Step N \u2192 Final Graph\n```\n\nEach step is independent, composable, and testable.\n\n### 10.2 Visitor Pattern\n\n`GraphWalker` visits each node and executes it:\n\n```go\ntype GraphWalker interface {\n    Execute(EvalContext, GraphNodeExecutable)\n}\n```\n\nAllows flexible execution strategies (sequential, parallel, with caching, etc.)\n\n### 10.3 Strategy Pattern\n\nOperation-specific behavior through factories:\n\n```go\n// Plan operation\nconcretePlan := func(a *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex {\n    return &NodePlanResourceInstance{...}\n}\n\n// Apply operation\nconcreteApply := func(a *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex {\n    return &NodeApplyResourceInstance{...}\n}\n```\n\n### 10.4 Template Method Pattern\n\nAbstract nodes define the template, concrete nodes implement steps:\n\n```go\ntype NodeAbstractResourceInstance struct {\n    // Common attributes\n    Addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n\n    // Implemented by concrete nodes\n    Execute() // Defined in NodePlanResourceInstance, etc.\n}\n```\n\n### 10.5 Observer Pattern\n\nHooks observe execution:\n\n```go\nHook interface {\n    PreApply(...)\n    PostApply(...)\n    // ... other observation points\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform's plan/apply architecture is built on these key principles:\n\n1. **Graph-Based Execution**: Dependencies drive parallelism\n2. **Phase Separation**: Planning and application are distinct phases\n3. **Plugin Architecture**: Providers implement resource operations\n4. **Thread-Safe State**: SyncState enables concurrent execution\n5. **Extensible Design**: Transformers and hooks allow customization\n6. **Composable Components**: Each piece is testable and replaceable\n7. **Error Isolation**: Failures don't corrupt state\n8. **Transparent Execution**: Hooks enable observation and control\n\nThis architecture enables Terraform to handle complex infrastructure as code scenarios with reliability, performance, and extensibility.\n",
  "file_path": "/workspace/documentation.md"

{
  "content": "# Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform's plan and apply operations are executed through a sophisticated graph-based execution engine. The architecture decomposes these operations into two major phases:\n\n1. **Graph Construction Phase**: Builds a directed acyclic graph (DAG) representing resources, their configurations, and their dependencies\n2. **Graph Execution Phase**: Traverses the graph respecting dependencies, executing operations in parallel where possible\n\nThis document details the internal architecture of these components and their interactions.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Graph Builder System\n\n### 1.1 Core Graph Structure\n\nThe `Graph` type represents the execution plan as a directed acyclic graph with the following structure:\n\n```\nGraph\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 dag.AcyclicGraph (embedded)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 Path: addrs.ModuleInstance  // Module scope for this graph\n```\n\n**Key Responsibilities:**\n- Maintains graph vertices (nodes) and edges (dependencies)\n- Validates that the graph is acyclic and has a single root\n- Provides traversal capabilities via the embedded `AcyclicGraph`\n- Supports concurrent graph walks through the `Walk()` method\n\n### 1.2 GraphBuilder Interface\n\nThe `GraphBuilder` interface defines how graphs are constructed:\n\n```go\ntype GraphBuilder interface {\n    Build(addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n}\n```\n\nThe standard implementation is `BasicGraphBuilder`, which:\n- Maintains an ordered list of `GraphTransformer` steps\n- Executes each transformer in sequence, modifying the graph incrementally\n- Validates the final graph for cycles and connectivity\n- Logs graph state changes after each transformation step\n\n**Execution Pattern:**\n```\nGraphBuilder.Build()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Create empty Graph\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 For each GraphTransformer in Steps:\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Call Transform(graph)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Log graph state\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Handle errors\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 Validate graph (single root, no cycles)\n```\n\n### 1.3 Phase-Specific Graph Builders\n\n#### PlanGraphBuilder\n\nConstructs the execution graph for plan operations. Key characteristics:\n\n- **Source of Truth**: Configuration (desired state) combined with current state\n- **Decisions Based On**: Diff between prior state and configuration\n- **Does NOT Consider**: Lifecycle preferences like `create_before_destroy` (these are post-plan concerns)\n\n**Key Fields:**\n- `Config`: Configuration tree representing desired state\n- `State`: Current state\n- `RootVariableValues`: Input variables provided by user\n- `Targets`: Resource targeting filters\n- `ForceReplace`: Resources to force replacement\n- `Plugins`: Provider and provisioner factory references\n\n#### ApplyGraphBuilder\n\nConstructs the execution graph for apply operations. Key characteristics:\n\n- **Source of Truth**: The Plan object (list of changes)\n- **Protects Against**: Applying resources not explicitly in the plan\n- **Decisions Based On**: The calculated changes from planning\n\n**Key Fields:**\n- `Config`: Configuration (must match the plan's source config)\n- `Changes`: The plan changes to apply\n- `State`: Current state before applying changes\n- `Targets`: Resource targeting filters (for consistency checking)\n\n### 1.4 Graph Transformers\n\nGraph transformers implement the `GraphTransformer` interface:\n\n```go\ntype GraphTransformer interface {\n    Transform(*Graph) error\n}\n```\n\nTransformers incrementally build the execution graph by:\n1. **Adding nodes**: Creating graph vertices representing resources, providers, modules, etc.\n2. **Creating edges**: Establishing dependency relationships\n3. **Filtering**: Removing nodes that shouldn't be executed\n4. **Expanding**: Converting abstract nodes to concrete operational nodes\n\n#### Key Transformer Categories\n\n**Configuration Transformers:**\n- `ConfigTransformer`: Adds all resources from configuration to graph\n- `AttachConfigProviderTransformer`: Attaches provider configuration to nodes\n- `AttachConfigResourceTransformer`: Attaches resource configuration to resource nodes\n- `AttachSchemaTransformer`: Adds provider schemas for validation\n\n**State Transformers:**\n- `AttachStateTransformer`: Attaches prior state to resource nodes\n- `StateTransformer`: Adds state-only resources not in configuration (for cleanup)\n\n**Expansion Transformers:**\n- `ExpandTransformer`: Expands `count` and `for_each` resources into concrete instances\n- `ModuleExpansionTransformer`: Expands module calls into concrete module instances\n- These are critical for dynamic expansion during execution\n\n**Dependency Transformers:**\n- `ReferenceTransformer`: Builds edges based on resource references in expressions\n- `ProviderTransformer`: Adds provider nodes and establishes provider dependencies\n- `DestroyEdgeTransformer`: Creates special edges for resource destruction order\n- `DestroyCreateBeforeDestroyTransformer`: Implements lifecycle rules\n\n**Filtering Transformers:**\n- `TargetsTransformer`: Filters graph to only targeted resources and their dependencies\n- `OrphanTransformer`: Marks resources for destruction if removed from configuration\n- `TransitiveReductionTransformer`: Removes redundant edges to simplify execution\n\n**Ordering Transformers:**\n- `ImportStateTransformer`: Adds import operations\n- `CheckTransformer`: Adds check validation nodes\n- `VariableValidationTransformer`: Adds variable validation nodes\n\n### 1.5 Node Types and Abstraction\n\n#### Abstract Nodes\n\nAbstract nodes are transitional node types that represent the logical concept of an operation without being executable:\n\n- `NodeAbstractResource`: Base for resource-level operations\n- `NodeAbstractResourceInstance`: Base for single resource instance operations\n- `NodeAbstractProvider`: Base for provider operations\n- `NodeAbstractModule`: Base for module operations\n\n**Concrete Node Conversion:**\n\nThe graph builder uses factory functions to convert abstract nodes to concrete, executable types:\n\n```go\n// Factory function signature\ntype ConcreteResourceInstanceNodeFunc func(*NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex\n\n// Usage in builders\nconcreteResourceInstance := func(a *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex {\n    return &NodeApplyableResourceInstance{\n        NodeAbstractResourceInstance: a,\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis allows the same abstract representation to be converted to different executable nodes depending on the operation (plan vs apply).\n\n#### Concrete Node Examples\n\n- `NodeApplyableResource`: Expansion node for apply phase\n- `NodePlanResourceInstance`: Plans changes for a resource instance\n- `NodeApplyableResourceInstance`: Applies a change to a resource instance\n- `NodeDestroyResourceInstance`: Destroys a resource instance\n- `NodeRefreshResourceInstance`: Refreshes a resource instance's state\n- `NodeApplyableProvider`: Initializes and configures a provider\n- `NodeDataSource`: Reads a data source\n- `NodeOutput`: Computes output values\n\n---\n\n## 2. Provider Interface and Lifecycle\n\n### 2.1 Provider Initialization and Management\n\nProviders are lazily initialized during graph execution through the `EvalContext` interface.\n\n#### Initialization Sequence\n\n```\n1. Provider node execution begins\n2. EvalContext.InitProvider(addr, config) called\n3. Provider plugin loaded and instantiated\n4. Provider schema retrieved from plugin\n5. Provider stored in cache for reuse\n6. Subsequent references use cached provider\n```\n\n#### Key EvalContext Methods for Providers\n\n```go\ntype EvalContext interface {\n    // Initialize a provider with configuration\n    InitProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config *configs.Provider)\n        (providers.Interface, error)\n\n    // Retrieve already-initialized provider\n    Provider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) providers.Interface\n\n    // Get provider schema (must already be initialized)\n    ProviderSchema(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) (providers.ProviderSchema, error)\n\n    // Close provider connections when done\n    CloseProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) error\n\n    // Configure provider with merged config\n    ConfigureProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config cty.Value) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n### 2.2 Provider Configuration and Input\n\nProvider configuration is built by merging multiple sources:\n\n```\nProvider Configuration = User Input + Explicit Config + Parent Config\n```\n\n**Priority Order:**\n1. User input from interactive prompts (highest priority)\n2. Explicit configuration from HCL\n3. Parent provider configuration (for child modules)\n\nThe `buildProviderConfig()` function handles this merging:\n\n```go\nfunc buildProviderConfig(ctx EvalContext, addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig,\n    config *configs.Provider) hcl.Body {\n    // Merge input and explicit config\n    // User input takes priority\n}\n```\n\n### 2.3 Provider Plugin Architecture\n\nProviders are external plugins communicating via gRPC. The plugin lifecycle:\n\n1. **Discovery**: Providers found in `.terraform/plugins` or installed via provider requirements\n2. **Loading**: Plugin binary launched as subprocess\n3. **Handshake**: Protocol negotiation and capability discovery\n4. **Schema Fetch**: Request provider schema definition\n5. **Configuration**: Provider receives merged configuration\n6. **Resource Operations**: Provider executes Create/Read/Update/Delete operations\n7. **Cleanup**: Provider process terminates when `CloseProvider()` called\n\n### 2.4 Resource Operation Delegation\n\nWhen a resource operation is planned or applied:\n\n```\nNode.Execute()\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Get provider from EvalContext\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Request resource schema from provider\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Build request object (state + config)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Call provider method (PlanResourceChange, ApplyResourceChange, etc.)\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Capture response (planned/new state, error)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 Update local state with response\n```\n\nEach provider method is responsible for:\n- Validating arguments\n- Computing differences (for Plan)\n- Making API calls\n- Handling errors\n- Returning updated resource state\n\n---\n\n## 3. State Management\n\n### 3.1 State Structure\n\nThe `State` type represents Terraform's persistent state:\n\n```\nState\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 Modules: map[string]*Module\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Module (for each module instance)\n\u2502       \u251c\u2500\u2500 Resources: map[string]*Resource\n\u2502       \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Resource\n\u2502       \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 Instances: map[addrs.InstanceKey]*ResourceInstance\n\u2502       \u2502           \u2514\u2500\u2500 ResourceInstance\n\u2502       \u2502               \u251c\u2500\u2500 Current: *ResourceInstanceObject\n\u2502       \u2502               \u2514\u2500\u2500 Deposed: map[DeposedKey]*ResourceInstanceObject\n\u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 Outputs: map[string]*OutputValue\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 RootOutputValues: map[string]*OutputValue\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 CheckResults: *CheckResults\n```\n\n**Key Properties:**\n- **Hierarchical**: Organized by modules and resources\n- **Instance-Based**: Resources can have multiple instances (count/for_each)\n- **Deposed Objects**: Tracks old objects during create-before-destroy operations\n- **Immutable Interface**: State should only be modified through `SyncState` methods\n\n### 3.2 State Synchronization (SyncState)\n\nFor concurrent graph execution, state is wrapped in `SyncState`:\n\n```go\ntype SyncState struct {\n    state    *State\n    writable bool\n    lock     sync.RWMutex  // Protects concurrent access\n}\n```\n\n**Features:**\n- Atomic operations: Multiple state changes happen together or not at all\n- Read-Write separation: Multiple readers or single writer\n- Deep copying: Returned values are independent copies\n- Automatic pruning: Empty modules are removed (except root)\n\n**High-Level Operations:**\n\n```go\n// Resource instance operations\nSetResourceInstanceCurrent(addr, obj, provider)\nDeposeResourceInstanceObject(addr) DeposedKey\nSetResourceInstanceDeposed(addr, key, obj, provider)\n\n// Output operations\nSetOutputValue(addr, value, sensitive)\nRemoveOutputValue(addr)\n\n// Module operations\nRemoveModule(addr)\n\n// Batch operations for planning\nUpdateResourceInstanceObjects(...)\n```\n\n**Benefits:**\n- Enables concurrent graph node execution without race conditions\n- Provides consistent snapshots for reading\n- Prevents partial state updates during failures\n\n### 3.3 Multiple State Versions During Execution\n\nTerraform maintains multiple state objects simultaneously during a walk:\n\n```\nState: Current state being built\n    \u2191\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 Updated by Apply/Plan nodes\n\nRefreshState: State after refresh phase\n    \u2191\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 Populated during refresh walk\n\nPrevRunState: State from previous run\n    \u2191\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 Loaded at start, used for comparison\n```\n\n**Usage:**\n- `State`: Primary state being modified\n- `RefreshState`: Previous state snapshot (for change detection)\n- `PrevRunState`: Used for comparisons and understanding drift\n\nThis enables:\n- Change detection: Compare current vs previous state\n- Rollback capability: Previous state preserved\n- Consistency checking: Ensure applied changes match plan\n\n### 3.4 State Persistence and Backends\n\nState management is abstracted through the state manager interface in `statemgr` package:\n\n```\nBackend (e.g., S3, Azure Storage)\n    \u2191\nState Manager (implements locking, versioning)\n    \u2191\nLocal State File (JSON format)\n```\n\n**Key Responsibilities:**\n- **Reading**: Load state from backend\n- **Locking**: Prevent concurrent operations\n- **Versioning**: Track state history\n- **Persistence**: Write updated state back to backend\n\nThe Context holds a reference to the state manager for:\n- Initial state loading\n- Atomic write-back after successful apply\n- Lock management during operations\n\n---\n\n## 4. Execution Flow and Hook System\n\n### 4.1 Overall Plan Execution Flow\n\n```\nContext.Plan(config, opts)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 1. Build Plan Graph\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 PlanGraphBuilder.Build()\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Apply transformers in sequence\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Return executable Graph\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 2. Refresh Walk (optional)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Walk graph with RefreshWalker\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Call resource ReadState for current values\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Update RefreshState with current values\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Returns refreshed state for comparison\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 3. Plan Walk\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Walk graph with PlanWalker\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 For each resource node:\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Call provider.PlanResourceChange()\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Capture planned change (Create/Update/Delete/NoOp)\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Store in Changes\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Returns complete change set\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500 4. Return Plan Object\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 Contains all changes ready for apply\n```\n\n### 4.2 Overall Apply Execution Flow\n\n```\nContext.Apply(plan, config, opts)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 1. Build Apply Graph\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 ApplyGraphBuilder.Build(plan.Changes)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Only includes changed resources\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Applies create-before-destroy ordering\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Return executable Graph\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 2. Apply Walk\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Walk graph with ApplyWalker\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 For each resource change node:\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Call provider resource operation (Create/Update/Delete)\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Update state with result\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Call hooks (PreApply, PostApply)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Handle deposed objects cleanup\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Update State atomically\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500 3. Return Updated State\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 State persisted to backend\n```\n\n### 4.3 Graph Traversal (Walker)\n\nThe DAG walker executes nodes respecting dependencies:\n\n```\nWalker Algorithm:\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 For each vertex (node) in graph:\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Wait for all dependencies to complete\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 If dependency failed: Skip or error (per graph semantics)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Execute node callback (concurrent if possible)\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Collect diagnostics\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Mark vertex complete\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500 Return aggregated diagnostics from all vertices\n```\n\n**Key Walker Characteristics:**\n- **Parallel Execution**: Independent nodes execute concurrently\n- **Dependency Respect**: Nodes only execute after upstream dependencies complete\n- **Atomic Failures**: Failed nodes block downstream dependents\n- **Cancelable**: Graph walk can be stopped via context cancellation\n\n### 4.4 Execution in ContextGraphWalker\n\nThe `ContextGraphWalker` implements the Terraform-specific walker pattern:\n\n```go\ntype ContextGraphWalker struct {\n    Context              *Context\n    State                *states.SyncState    // Main state\n    RefreshState         *states.SyncState    // Pre-walk state snapshot\n    Changes              *plans.ChangesSync   // Accumulates changes\n    Checks               *checks.State\n    NamedValues          *namedvals.State     // Variable/output tracking\n    InstanceExpander     *instances.Expander  // Count/for_each expansion\n    Operation            walkOperation\n    StopContext          context.Context\n}\n\n// Key method called for each node\nfunc (w *ContextGraphWalker) Execute(ctx EvalContext, node GraphNodeExecutable) {\n    // Acquire parallelism semaphore\n    w.Context.parallelSem.Acquire()\n    defer w.Context.parallelSem.Release()\n\n    // Execute the node\n    return node.Execute(ctx, w.Operation)\n}\n```\n\n**Scope Management:**\n\nThe walker maintains multiple evaluation contexts, one per module:\n\n```go\nfunc (w *ContextGraphWalker) enterScope(scope evalContextScope) EvalContext {\n    // Returns EvalContext scoped to a specific module\n    // Caches contexts to ensure consistency\n}\n```\n\nThis allows:\n- Module isolation\n- Variable scope containment\n- Provider configuration inheritance\n\n### 4.5 Hook System\n\nHooks are callback points allowing external code to observe and influence execution.\n\n#### Hook Interface\n\n```go\ntype Hook interface {\n    // Resource operation hooks\n    PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        newState cty.Value, err error) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Plan hooks\n    PreDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        priorState, proposedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey,\n        action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Provisioning hooks\n    PreProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PreProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string, err error) (HookAction, error)\n    ProvisionOutput(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string, line string)\n\n    // State refresh hooks\n    PreRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState, newState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Import hooks\n    PreImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, importID string) (HookAction, error)\n    PostImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, imported []providers.ImportedResource) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Lifecycle hooks\n    PostStateUpdate(new *states.State) (HookAction, error)\n    Stopping()\n}\n```\n\n#### Hook Actions\n\n```go\ntype HookAction byte\n\nconst (\n    HookActionContinue  // Proceed normally\n    HookActionHalt      // Cancel operation\n)\n```\n\n#### Hook Execution Flow\n\n```\nFor each hook in Context.hooks:\n    Call hook method with resource details\n    \u251c\u2500 HookActionContinue: Proceed to next hook\n    \u2514\u2500 HookActionHalt: Cancel operation, stop remaining hooks\n```\n\n#### Common Hook Uses\n\n1. **UI Output**: Display resource operations and status\n2. **Logging**: Track operations for audit\n3. **Monitoring**: Integrate with external systems\n4. **Validation**: Custom checks during apply\n5. **Deferral**: Implement custom pause/resume logic\n\n### 4.6 Dynamic Expansion During Execution\n\nCount and for_each resources are expanded dynamically during graph execution.\n\n#### Instance Expansion\n\n```\nInstance Expander tracks:\n\u251c\u2500 count.index / each.key / each.value for current iteration\n\u251c\u2500 length calculations for count\n\u251c\u2500 map iterations for for_each\n\u2514\u2500 Nested expansion for resource instances\n```\n\n**Expansion Process:**\n\n```\n1. InstanceExpander node executes\n   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Evaluates count or for_each expression\n   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Creates abstract instances for each value\n\n2. Instance keys created: IntKey for count, StringKey for for_each\n\n3. Per-instance nodes created from abstract node\n   \u251c\u2500\u2500 NodeResourcePlanInstance\n   \u251c\u2500\u2500 NodeResourceApplyInstance\n   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Can access instance key for self references\n\n4. Instances execute in graph order\n   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Each instance has independent state/attributes\n```\n\n**Data Available to Instances:**\n\n```\nself.*              // Current resource's computed attributes\ncount.index         // Numeric index (count)\neach.key            // Map key (for_each)\neach.value          // Map value (for_each)\nresource.*.id       // Splat referencing other instances\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Evaluation Context\n\n### 5.1 EvalContext Interface\n\nThe `EvalContext` is the primary interface for node execution, providing access to:\n\n```go\ntype EvalContext interface {\n    // Module and path information\n    Path() addrs.ModuleInstance\n    Stopped() <-chan struct{}\n\n    // Provider operations\n    InitProvider(addr, config) providers.Interface\n    Provider(addr) providers.Interface\n    ProviderSchema(addr) providers.ProviderSchema\n    CloseProvider(addr) error\n    ConfigureProvider(addr, config) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n    // Provisioners\n    Provisioner(name) provisioners.Interface\n    ProvisionerSchema(name) *configschema.Block\n\n    // State and changes\n    State() *states.SyncState\n    RefreshState() *states.SyncState\n    Changes() *plans.ChangesSync\n    NamedValues() *namedvals.State\n\n    // Expression evaluation\n    EvaluateBlock(body, schema, self, key) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n    EvaluateExpr(expr, wantType, self) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n    EvaluationScope(self, source, key) *lang.Scope\n\n    // Hooks and plugins\n    Hook(callback func(Hook) error) error\n    Input() UIInput\n}\n```\n\n### 5.2 BuiltinEvalContext Implementation\n\nThe standard implementation provides:\n\n```go\ntype BuiltinEvalContext struct {\n    // Execution environment\n    StopContext  context.Context\n    InstanceExpander *instances.Expander\n\n    // Caches\n    ProviderCache      map[string]providers.Interface\n    ProvisionerCache   map[string]provisioners.Interface\n\n    // State and configuration\n    StateValue         *states.SyncState\n    ChangesValue       *plans.ChangesSync\n    ChecksValue        *checks.State\n    NamedValuesValue   *namedvals.State\n    DeferralsValue     *deferring.Deferred\n\n    // Configuration\n    ConfigValue        *configs.Config\n    PluginsValue       *contextPlugins\n\n    // Evaluation\n    EvaluatorValue     *Evaluator\n}\n```\n\n**Key Responsibilities:**\n- Maintains caches for provider/provisioner instances\n- Coordinates access to state and changes\n- Provides expression evaluation capabilities\n- Manages hook invocation\n\n### 5.3 Evaluation and Expression Handling\n\nThe `Evaluator` handles HCL expression evaluation:\n\n```\nExpression Evaluation:\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Parse expression as HCL\n\u251c\u2500 Build evaluation scope with:\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Module variables\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Local values\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Resource references\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 Data source references\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 Functions and operators\n\u251c\u2500 Execute evaluation in scope\n\u251c\u2500 Apply type conversion if needed\n\u2514\u2500 Return evaluated cty.Value\n```\n\n**Scope Includes:**\n- `self.*`: Current resource or data source\n- Variables from root and current module\n- Outputs from all modules\n- Data source read values\n- Locals from current module\n- References to other resources/data sources\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points\n\n### 6.1 Custom Transformers\n\nExtend graph building by implementing `GraphTransformer`:\n\n```go\ntype CustomTransformer struct {\n    // Configuration\n}\n\nfunc (t *CustomTransformer) Transform(g *Graph) error {\n    // Add, remove, or modify nodes and edges\n    return nil\n}\n\n// Register with graph builder\nbuilder.Steps = append(builder.Steps, &CustomTransformer{})\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Custom node scheduling\n- Integration-specific resource ordering\n- Cost optimization by graph reordering\n- Security enforcement via forced dependencies\n\n### 6.2 Custom Hooks\n\nImplement `Hook` interface to observe execution:\n\n```go\ntype CustomHook struct{\n}\n\nfunc (h *CustomHook) PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, ...) (HookAction, error) {\n    // Log, validate, or modify behavior\n    return HookActionContinue, nil\n}\n\n// Register with context\nopts.Hooks = append(opts.Hooks, &CustomHook{})\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Real-time operation monitoring\n- Cost estimation\n- Resource validation\n- Event forwarding to external systems\n- Custom approval workflows\n\n### 6.3 Provider Plugins\n\nProviders are the primary extension point. Implement the `providers.Interface`:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    GetSchema(ctx context.Context) (*ProviderSchema, error)\n    PrepareProviderConfig(ctx context.Context, req PrepareProviderConfigRequest) PrepareProviderConfigResponse\n    ValidateResourceConfig(ctx context.Context, req ValidateResourceConfigRequest) ValidateResourceConfigResponse\n    ReadResource(ctx context.Context, req ReadResourceRequest) ReadResourceResponse\n    PlanResourceChange(ctx context.Context, req PlanResourceChangeRequest) PlanResourceChangeResponse\n    ApplyResourceChange(ctx context.Context, req ApplyResourceChangeRequest) ApplyResourceChangeResponse\n    // ... more methods\n}\n```\n\n**Hook Points:**\n- Configuration validation\n- Resource diffing\n- Resource creation, update, deletion\n- State refresh\n- Data source reads\n\n### 6.4 Custom Provisioners\n\nImplement `provisioners.Interface` for post-apply provisioning:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    GetSchema(ctx context.Context) (*configschema.Block, error)\n    ProvisionResource(ctx context.Context, req ProvisionResourceRequest) ProvisionResourceResponse\n    Stop(ctx context.Context) error\n}\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Configuration management (Ansible, Chef, Puppet)\n- Custom deployment scripts\n- Infrastructure validation\n- Service registration\n\n---\n\n## 7. Error Handling\n\n### 7.1 Error Propagation\n\nErrors are collected and propagated through the execution flow:\n\n```\nNode.Execute() returns tfdiags.Diagnostics\n    \u2193\nDiagnostic collected in walker\n    \u2193\nWalker stops dependent nodes\n    \u2193\nAggregated diagnostics returned to caller\n```\n\n**Diagnostic Types:**\n- `Error`: Prevents operation and downstream nodes\n- `Warning`: Logged but doesn't block execution\n- `Detail`: Informational messages\n\n### 7.2 Failure Handling in Parallel Execution\n\nWhen a node fails:\n\n1. **Downstream Blocking**: Dependent nodes receive error signal and don't execute\n2. **Parallel Sibling Isolation**: Independent nodes continue executing\n3. **Partial Completion**: Some resources may have executed before failure\n4. **State Preservation**: State partially updated with successful operations\n\n**Recovery Strategy:**\n- User can fix error and rerun plan/apply\n- Partial state is not persisted without full success\n- Deferred resources allow deferring problematic resources to next run\n\n### 7.3 Non-Fatal Errors\n\nSome errors don't block execution:\n\n```go\ntype NonFatalError interface {\n    Diagnostics() tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\nThese allow:\n- Collection of multiple issues\n- User fixing issues in one pass\n- Proceeding with partial results when appropriate\n\n---\n\n## 8. Data Flow Diagram\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Configuration  \u2502\n\u2502   (HCL files)   \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n         \u2502\n         v\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502  Config Loader          \u2502\n\u2502  (parses, validates)    \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n         \u2502\n         v\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 Graph Builder           \u2502\n\u2502 (PlanGraphBuilder)      \u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2524\n\u2502 Steps:                  \u2502\n\u2502 1. ConfigTransformer    \u2502\n\u2502 2. ExpandTransformer    \u2502\n\u2502 3. ReferenceTransformer \u2502\n\u2502 4. ProviderTransformer  \u2502\n\u2502 5. ... (more)           \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n Concrete Node Conversion      \u2502\n\u2502 (factories apply) \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n---\n\n## 9. Performance Considerations\n\n### 9.1 Parallelism\n\nGraph execution naturally parallelizes:\n\n**Without Dependencies**: 100 independent resources execute concurrently (up to parallelism limit)\n\n**With Dependencies**: Resources execute in dependency order, but siblings execute in parallel\n\n```\nExample:\naws_vpc.main (Parallelism: 1/10)\n\u251c\u2500 aws_subnet.a (Parallelism: 2/10)\n\u251c\u2500 aws_subnet.b (Parallelism: 3/10)\n\u2514\u2500 aws_subnet.c (Parallelism: 4/10)\n   \u251c\u2500 aws_instance.1 (Parallelism: 5/10)\n   \u251c\u2500 aws_instance.2 (Parallelism: 6/10)\n   \u2514\u2500 aws_instance.3 (Parallelism: 7/10)\n```\n\n### 9.2 State Access Optimization\n\n`SyncState` minimizes lock contention:\n\n- Atomic operations reduce lock time\n- Deep copies prevent concurrent mutations\n- Module-level granularity allows targeting\n- Read-write separation maximizes parallelism\n\n### 9.3 Graph Construction Time\n\nLarge graphs (100s of resources) build in milliseconds:\n\n- Transformers run sequentially (single-threaded)\n- Most transformers run in O(n) or O(n log n)\n- TransitiveReduction can be expensive (O(VE)) but optional\n\n### 9.4 Execution Time Optimization Opportunities\n\n1. **Targeted apply**: Only resources with changes\n2. **Parallelism tuning**: `-parallelism=N` flag\n3. **Resource ordering**: Explicit `depends_on` for critical paths\n4. **Deferred actions**: Postpone problematic resources\n5. **Caching**: Provider schemas cached, reused across module instances\n\n---\n\n## 10. Key Architectural Patterns\n\n### 10.1 Builder Pattern\n\nThe `BasicGraphBuilder` + `GraphTransformer` chain:\n\n```\nEmpty Graph \u2192 Step 1 \u2192 Step 2 \u2192 ... \u2192 Step N \u2192 Final Graph\n```\n\nEach step is independent, composable, and testable.\n\n### 10.2 Visitor Pattern\n\n`GraphWalker` visits each node and executes it:\n\n```go\ntype GraphWalker interface {\n    Execute(EvalContext, GraphNodeExecutable)\n}\n```\n\nAllows flexible execution strategies (sequential, parallel, with caching, etc.)\n\n### 10.3 Strategy Pattern\n\nOperation-specific behavior through factories:\n\n```go\n// Plan operation\nconcretePlan := func(a *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex {\n    return &NodePlanResourceInstance{...}\n}\n\n// Apply operation\nconcreteApply := func(a *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) dag.Vertex {\n    return &NodeApplyResourceInstance{...}\n}\n```\n\n### 10.4 Template Method Pattern\n\nAbstract nodes define the template, concrete nodes implement steps:\n\n```go\ntype NodeAbstractResourceInstance struct {\n    // Common attributes\n    Addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance\n\n    // Implemented by concrete nodes\n    Execute() // Defined in NodePlanResourceInstance, etc.\n}\n```\n\n### 10.5 Observer Pattern\n\nHooks observe execution:\n\n```go\nHook interface {\n    PreApply(...)\n    PostApply(...)\n    // ... other observation points\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform's plan/apply architecture is built on these key principles:\n\n1. **Graph-Based Execution**: Dependencies drive parallelism\n2. **Phase Separation**: Planning and application are distinct phases\n3. **Plugin Architecture**: Providers implement resource operations\n4. **Thread-Safe State**: SyncState enables concurrent execution\n5. **Extensible Design**: Transformers and hooks allow customization\n6. **Composable Components**: Each piece is testable and replaceable\n7. **Error Isolation**: Failures don't corrupt state\n8. **Transparent Execution**: Hooks enable observation and control\n\nThis architecture enables Terraform to handle complex infrastructure as code scenarios with reliability, performance, and extensibility.\n",

# Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture

## Overview

Terraform's plan and apply operations are executed through a sophisticated graph-based execution engine. The architecture decomposes these operations into two major phases:

1. **Graph Construction Phase**: Builds a directed acyclic graph (DAG) representing resources, their configurations, and their dependencies
2. **Graph Execution Phase**: Traverses the graph respecting dependencies, executing operations in parallel where possible

This document details the internal architecture of these components and their interactions.

---

## 1. Graph Builder System

### 1.1 Core Graph Structure

The `Graph` type represents the execution plan as a directed acyclic graph with the following structure:

```
Graph
├── dag.AcyclicGraph (embedded)
└── Path: addrs.ModuleInstance  // Module scope for this graph
```

**Key Responsibilities:**
- Maintains graph vertices (nodes) and edges (dependencies)
- Validates that the graph is acyclic and has a single root
- Provides traversal capabilities via the embedded `AcyclicGraph`
- Supports concurrent graph walks through the `Walk()` method

### 1.2 GraphBuilder Interface

The `GraphBuilder` interface defines how graphs are constructed:

```go
type GraphBuilder interface {
    Build(addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics)
}
```

The standard implementation is `BasicGraphBuilder`, which:
- Maintains an ordered list of `GraphTransformer` steps
- Executes each transformer in sequence, modifying the graph incrementally
- Validates the final graph for cycles and connectivity
- Logs graph state changes after each transformation step

**Execution Pattern:**
```
GraphBuilder.Build()
├── Create empty Graph
├── For each GraphTransformer in Steps:
│   ├── Call Transform(graph)
│   ├──
... (truncated)
